    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer18140161706187681861"><i>This whole grim reaper thing should have come with a manual.<br/>Or a diagram of some kind.<br/>A flow chart would have been nice.</i><p>Charley Davidson is a part-time private investigator and full-time grim reaper. Meaning, she sees dead people. Really. And it's her job to convince them to "go into the light." But when these very dead people have died under less than ideal circumstances </p></span>
  <span id="freeText18140161706187681861" style="display:none"><i>This whole grim reaper thing should have come with a manual.<br />Or a diagram of some kind.<br />A flow chart would have been nice.</i><p>Charley Davidson is a part-time private investigator and full-time grim reaper. Meaning, she sees dead people. Really. And it's her job to convince them to "go into the light." But when these very dead people have died under less than ideal circumstances (like murder), sometimes they want Charley to bring the bad guys to justice. Complicating matters are the intensely hot dreams she's been having about an entity who has been following her all her life...and it turns out he might not be dead after all. In fact, he might be something else entirely. But what does he want with Charley? And why can't she seem to resist him? And what does she have to lose by giving in?</p><p>With scorching-hot tension and high-octane humor, <i>First Grave on the Right</i> is your signpost to paranormal suspense of the highest order.</p></span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You should absolutely give this book a chance. It's a funny and easy read with it's serious moments. Try the audible edition if you like listening to <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You should absolutely give this book a chance. It's a funny and easy read with it's serious moments. Try the audible edition if you like listening to audiobooks. The narrator is one of the best and does a terrific job bringing the characters to life.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_355138830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355138830" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355138830?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355138830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9646205296056165531"><b>Charley Davidson is like white chocolate. You either love it, or you think it's an abomination of nature.</b> I love white chocolate, I love Charley Davidson, and I am not ashamed.<br/><br/>She's got such a great narrative voice - she is, dare I say it, a lot like me. A lot of deadpan humor. A lot of inappropriate thoughts at the worst possible times.<blockquote>
  <i>“Well, I was kind of kidnapped, though not really kidnapped so much as led away.”<br/><br/>A hand shot to her mouth to squelch a gasp.<br/><br/>“God, all this sounds so awful whe</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9646205296056165531" style="display:none"><b>Charley Davidson is like white chocolate. You either love it, or you think it's an abomination of nature.</b> I love white chocolate, I love Charley Davidson, and I am not ashamed.<br /><br />She's got such a great narrative voice - she is, dare I say it, a lot like me. A lot of deadpan humor. A lot of inappropriate thoughts at the worst possible times.<blockquote>
  <i>“Well, I was kind of kidnapped, though not really kidnapped so much as led away.”<br /><br />A hand shot to her mouth to squelch a gasp.<br /><br />“God, all this sounds so awful when I say it out loud,” I complained. “I whine more than a Goth with a blogging fetish. It’s really not that bad. I actually grew up rather happy. I had lots of friends. They were mostly dead, but still.”</i>
</blockquote>Charley is special without being a special snowflake.<blockquote>
  <i>“Is anything broken?” Uncle Bob’s voice had softened.<br /><br />“My eyelids, I think. I can’t open them.”<br /><br />I heard a soft chuckle. “If it were anyone else, I’d say eyelids can’t be broken. But considering the source…”<br /><br />A weak grin spread across my face. “So I’m, like, special?”<br /><br />He snorted as he pressed gingerly here and there, testing for broken bones and the like. “Special wouldn’t even begin to cover it, my dear.”</i>
</blockquote>Charley is a Grim Reaper. She can see the dead and take them through the other side. As you can well imagine, it must have been pretty fucking rough growing up with that ability. Seriously, some kid comes up to me and tells me <i>"I see dead people,"</i> you'd tell him he was nuts and eventually everyone else would pick up on the weirdness, because kids are assholes. Charley grew up ostracized by friends and even family, but she coped in her own way; she is strong, she is resilient. She isn't filled with misery and depression and self-pity. She is pissed off, at times, but she deals with it through her snark and sarcasm and all-around awesome Charley-ness. Which isn't to say she never gets angry, she damned well gets mad, but she can deal with the unfairness life has dealt her.<blockquote>
  <i>“People like those assholes at the station yesterday. People like Taft with their sideways glances and hushed whispers who turn their backs on me every time I walk into a room. People like you who treat me like shit until they figure out I really can do what I say I can do. And then suddenly I’m their best friend.”</i>
</blockquote>We all have our coping mechanism, and I see her sarcasm and her inappropriate sense of humor as one of such. Seriously, I find Charley absolutely hilarious. She speaks her lines with such a deadpan sense of humor. The first time I read the book, I was howling with laughter.<blockquote>
  <i>I twisted around in my seat to face him. “My fore-parts, as you so ineloquently put it, have names.” I pointed to my right breast. “This is Danger.” Then my left. “And this is Will Robinson. I would appreciate it if you addressed them accordingly.”<br /><br />After a long pause in which he took the time to blink several times, he asked, “You named your breasts?”<br /><br />I turned my back to him with a shrug. “I named my ovaries, too, but they don’t get out as much.</i>
</blockquote>I know that Charley isn't everyone's cup of tea, and I completely understand if she grates on your nerves, but personally, I adore her. (well, I can't say the same for the later books in the series, but still)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9646205296056165531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_154598906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154598906" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154598906?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=bleh">bleh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fluff-fluffy-fluffest">fluff-fluffy-fluffest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154598906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13736899637574660976">I think it's time someone let the author of this book into a little secret: Ms. Jones, stringing together a thousand-odd wisecracks does not make a novel. <i>That</i> is more commonly known as a Joke Book. In fiction, we like our wisecracks accompanied by an actual plot, plot development, sub-plots and character development. Say it with me, Sto-ry-line. <br/><br/>You know that teen movie trope about a nerdy guy trying to be popular by joking around with the jocks? Only his jokes always sound rehearsed and fall f</span>
  <span id="freeText13736899637574660976" style="display:none">I think it's time someone let the author of this book into a little secret: Ms. Jones, stringing together a thousand-odd wisecracks does not make a novel. <i>That</i> is more commonly known as a Joke Book. In fiction, we like our wisecracks accompanied by an actual plot, plot development, sub-plots and character development. Say it with me, Sto-ry-line. <br /><br />You know that teen movie trope about a nerdy guy trying to be popular by joking around with the jocks? Only his jokes always sound rehearsed and fall flat, and he fades away into obscurity?<br /><br />First Grave on the Right reminds me of nothing so much as that guy, trying desperately to be funny so people would be inclined to like him better and overlook his general lack of charisma. The book is filled with 'gems' like <i>Isn’t that a bit like the pot calling the kettle African-American?</i> and <i>If I were edible, I’d be a fruitcake.</i> <br />... no, <i>of course</i> I haven't heard that one before, ha ha.<br /><br />The only reason this book is getting two stars is because it actually managed to surprise some involuntary laughter out of me at some points. Here, for example:<br /><br /><i>[...] On the plus side, I did learn that Martians should never try to become human just to drink our water. Since Martians didn’t exist, I figured they were part of some bizarre Rocket Man analogy. So what on Earth could be comparable to alien beings? Besides circus performers? It had to be someone living contrary to the norm. I could think of a couple of groups, but I felt strangely secure in the knowledge that Reyes was neither an IRS auditor nor a member of the Manson family.</i><br /><br />But such truly witty moments are few and far. The rest of the book reads like one of those sitcoms where the only laughter generated is from a can. You never really get a feel for any of the characters sandwiched in between all the sarcasm. Even Charley Davidson end up being an amalgamation of unending snark, constant injury and metaphysical sexcapades. She’s so busy inserting self-deprecating humor into her backstory she fails to make an impact even at the points when she <i>should</i> have been hitting the emotional hot buttons. And do NOT get me started on the number of times she tells Garrett Swopes to kiss her ass! Seriously, I think he got it the first ten times you said it, Charley! <br /><br />The plot development is rudimentary, at best. Characters appear, and disappear without warning, and their absences are never explained satisfactorily. The book begins when Charley encounters the ghosts of three law firm partners in quick succession, all three lawyers having been killed by the same modus operandi, at the same time. So, of course, one would be justified in thinking that this mystery would form the crux of the ‘plot’. One would be wrong. About a quarter of the way through, Charley, in a classic display of self-diagnosed ADD, suddenly decides to abandon this mystery in favour of hunting down her mysterious dream lover. <br /><br />The lawyer-mystery involves mafiosi, human trafficking, murder, false imprisonment and missing teenagers. But of course, solving that is a piece of cake. It requires about fifty pages in the beginning, a little five-page teaser in the middle, and a convenient ten-page conclusion with next to no investigative input from Charley Davidson, PI. <br /><br />All of the grim reaper-slash-private investigator’s resources, through most of the book, are tied up in investigating the mystery man who has hot dream sex with her every night. Said dreamboat (ha! Pun!) is, of course, supernatural, super-hot, super-powerful, super-possessive, super-protective and consequently, <i>just</i> the sort of man every independent woman dreams of. Having started off their association on an auspicious note by strangling her in a chokehold and threatening to rape her, he then continues their happy, fulfilling relationship by vanishing for several decades before returning to dream-rape her anonymously. But hey, guess what, it’s all forgiven because he’s so hot and he’s saved her life several times, and the dream sex is so orgasmic, and she felt a ‘connection’ with him when he first assaulted and threatened her, and — did I mention — he’s SO HOT?!!<br /><br />Then there is the third angle in this painful triangle, the hot, human Garrett Swopes who pisses off our heroine by refusing to accept immediately that she can see ghosts. How very unreasonable and unromantic of him! No doubt, if he had pushed her up against the wall and threatened to whip her, she would have been more accepting of his measly human scruples! There are several heavy-handed hints that he likes Charley, but she remains madly in love with the man of her dreams. Who is in prison for murdering a man, but surprise, surprise, Charley just <i>knows</i> he didn’t do it! Why? Because <i>she</i> doesn’t believe he’s that kind of guy! I wonder why the defense didn’t present THAT argument during his trial?!<br /><br />There are several sub-plots that are very unnecessary, like the one about the client who tries to escape her abusive husband; ideally, this book would have worked way better if Jones had stuck to the Reyes storyline, eliminated the weak attempt at a stand-alone mystery, cut down on the canned sarcasm, and given her characters a personality. I cannot understand how Reyes could possibly be appealing? For almost all of the book, he is a dream-invading sex maniac who generally appears as a black blob and never says anything, and conveniently plays knight-in-black-cloud to Charley’s damsel in distress. Severing spines... the new route to winning hearts and seducing ladies! <br /><br />And the grand reveal at the end? SO unnecessary! The one thing this book had going for it was the fact that it was a fun, light-hearted read. To destroy that by introducing a grand battle between Heaven and Hell is just plain sad. Not to mention clichéd, and completely out of keeping with the irreverent tone of the rest of this book. <br /><br />All-in-all, a very forgettable book; I guess I would recommend it for a beach read, or for a very boring flight. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13736899637574660976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_791074494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791074494" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791074494?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9732753-first-grave-on-the-right">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791074494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12524048621040341245">You know, I love a well-written, well-constructed, complex urban fantasy world as much as anyone. I love beautiful writing, jam-packed plots and wild twists that I never would have seen coming. But sometimes, just sometimes, I have a real need for something lighthearted, nonsensical, silly and sexy. Like the Bridget Jones version of urban fantasy. Paranormal "chick lit" one might say. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson__1_' title='First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson #1) by Darynda Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>First Grave on the Right</a> is a girls' night in watching your all time favourite romcom whilst eating ice cream. I</span>
  <span id="freeText12524048621040341245" style="display:none">You know, I love a well-written, well-constructed, complex urban fantasy world as much as anyone. I love beautiful writing, jam-packed plots and wild twists that I never would have seen coming. But sometimes, just sometimes, I have a real need for something lighthearted, nonsensical, silly and sexy. Like the Bridget Jones version of urban fantasy. Paranormal "chick lit" one might say. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson__1_" title="First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson #1) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">First Grave on the Right</a> is a girls' night in watching your all time favourite romcom whilst eating ice cream. In your pajamas. It's pure, cookie dough-flavoured fun. It won't change your life. It won't introduce you to a new way of thinking. But, if you're anything like me, it might just hijack your mind and take it to happy land for a while. Here's what this book has: a sarcastic, witty and hilarious heroine; a sexy, mysterious guy; a murder mystery; and humour bursting from every page. <br><br>Oh, what the hell, why use words when I can say it with gifs. And seeing as I'm currently re-watching Buffy and it seems appropriate, I'm going to say it with Buffy gifs.<br><br><b>There's some:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387679742ra/7650010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And a touch of:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387679742ra/7650011.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And a whole lot of:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387679742ra/7650012.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And a bit more:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387679742ra/7650013.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Note to readers: you might want to turn your google filters on before searching "sexy gifs". Unless, of course, you don't.)<br><br>I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson__1_" title="First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson #1) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">First Grave on the Right</a> so much that I bought the rest of the series all at once (something I just don't normally do). I can see this being the kind of series that I'll need a regular fix of because it's delightfully addictive. I'm now getting started on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565045.Second_Grave_on_the_Left__Charley_Davidson__2_" title="Second Grave on the Left (Charley Davidson #2) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Second Grave on the Left</a> and I can't wait to see more of Charley's sarcasm, Reyes' sexiness, and the general demonic craziness going on. <br><br><b>*sigh* This was just what I needed.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12524048621040341245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_242439153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242439153" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242439153?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781427211309" href="/book/show/8788555-first-grave-on-the-right">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242439153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7527881344275081242">First my over all impression of this book. Then I'll give some detail as to why I feel as I do. I picked this up because it got a...."whole passel", of 4 and 5 star ratings here. My over all impression of the book????<br/><br/>It's crap.<br/><br/><br/>Why do I think that? Well at first I was thinking it would be okay if not one I really liked. It opened with an account of the protagonists dream where she was having intercourse with a "hot" shadowy figure. She made sure to tell us she'd had an orgasm.<br/><br/>I sighed and went on</span>
  <span id="freeText7527881344275081242" style="display:none">First my over all impression of this book. Then I'll give some detail as to why I feel as I do. I picked this up because it got a...."whole passel", of 4 and 5 star ratings here. My over all impression of the book????<br /><br />It's crap.<br /><br /><br />Why do I think that? Well at first I was thinking it would be okay if not one I really liked. It opened with an account of the protagonists dream where she was having intercourse with a "hot" shadowy figure. She made sure to tell us she'd had an orgasm.<br /><br />I sighed and went on. I can live with a little overt sex in a book if the author seems to think that it's important to the story. I can usually skim through it if it gets really graphic. And if it's really for the story you won't be getting a heavy or graphic sex scene every second page. This was more, "in your face" than graphic. It was a short intro passage and I figured it was to tell me what a "kick ass" female protagonist we had.<br /><br />Except that about every second page our female P.I./Grim reaper had to refer back to her hot dream. She had to be sure and tell me/us that she'd never had an orgasm in a dream before. She had to tell us about her shadowy lover's body parts etc.<br /><br />I sighed and moved past a lot.<br /><br />There is a bit of humor here but I didn't find the character as funny as some did...or as funny as she finds herself.<br /><br />Sadly, for me anyway, I did see the beginnings of an interesting story here, but the writer just couldn't or wouldn't stay with it. She kept swerving off to one side. The wise cracking heroine's story would draw me in and then crash.<br /><br />I can see that I might enjoy some things by this writer, but maybe I'm not the audience she's shooting for. Many love this book, their reviews and ratings are why I tried it (though my first look at the cover art when I picked this up at the library signaled me I might be barking up the wrong proverbial tree). I held on following the story and the side trails we were running down (at the point where I was in the book, I have no idea how many of the dead people we've encountered would have ended up being part of the main plot). BUT we came to a scene where I realized we'd gone a bridge too far for me. (I'll say below under a spoiler marker). I knew I didn't even want to follow the story any more it seems there is a device she's using (and of course some will disagree with me) that was something I didn't care for.<br /><br />So, 1 star because I can't go lower and I didn't finish the book... <br /><br />Now, what pushed me over the edge?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ As I said our heroine goes on at length about her "sex" life. Up to a point I was philosophical about it. I could take the commentary on men's butts and so on. Some feel that's just the female half of the population getting their own back a bit.<br /><br />But we came to a scene where we saw what was described as a "boy" being assaulted, possibly attempted murder....our protagonist intervenes (of course). Not to give the whole scene , but when she interacts with the "boy" he seems bigger. He wants her to stay out of it. He threatens her, he grabs her throat and pushes her back (okay at this point I had to realize the impression I had from the first mention that he was about 13 was wrong). When she insists that she will call the police anyway he asks her "have you ever been raped?" By the time he had his hand between her legs I'd put the book down, and don't plan to pick it up again. <br /><br />You who like this thing...enjoy. It's not for me. Possibly just me but I prefer that my light reading contain as few rapes and/or attempted rapes as possible.<br /><br />It seems to me that whenever things slow up a bit or there's a lull in the action the author goes for the groin. Not the best of literary devices.<br /><br />As I said if it's your cup of tea, enjoy. To me it seems to be going the way of the only Laural K. Hamilton book I've tried.<br /><br />Keep it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7527881344275081242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2578213994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2578213994" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2578213994?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2578213994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12602693437937119237">First Grave on the Right by Darynda Jones is a 2011 St. Martin’s Press publication. <br/><br/>Uproariously funny and Unique!! <br/><br/>This is the first book in the Charley Davidson series. I’ve noticed a few of my GR friends have read books in this series and it seems to be popular, but I was not sure about diving into a paranormal/ urban fantasy series after burning out on the genre during the ‘Twilight’ craze. So, I initially passed on it. <br/><br/>But, I am craving something otherworldly right now, so when I noticed a </span>
  <span id="freeText12602693437937119237" style="display:none">First Grave on the Right by Darynda Jones is a 2011 St. Martin’s Press publication. <br /><br />Uproariously funny and Unique!! <br /><br />This is the first book in the Charley Davidson series. I’ve noticed a few of my GR friends have read books in this series and it seems to be popular, but I was not sure about diving into a paranormal/ urban fantasy series after burning out on the genre during the ‘Twilight’ craze. So, I initially passed on it. <br /><br />But, I am craving something otherworldly right now, so when I noticed a new installment in this series was coming out soon, and picking up a little chatter, I decided to see if this one would be a good fit for me. <br /><br />If this first book is any indication, then I’d say I could fall completely under the Charley Davidson’s scathing, testy, and snappy spell.<br /><br />Charley is a private investigator and a grim reaper. By grim reaper I mean she is able to see dead people and her job is to lure them into the light. To convince them, she often has to help them find peace by discovering who murdered them or finally getting justice on their behalf. <br /><br />With the help of her uncle, a deceased former gang member named, Angel, and her best friend, Cookie, Charley solves crimes, and helps the dead pass over. But, in her personal life, she’s coping with an unseen entity that visits her dreams in a super- hot sensual way. Finding who and what this entity is that has followed her around her entire life is her most fervent wish. But, as they say- Be careful what you wish for! <br /><br />I’ve read urban fantasy stories that were light and funny, some that were serious and super dark, but I’ve never read one that mixed such sharp wit and gallows humor, with action, adventure, dark fantasy, and a genuine murder mystery before. But, that’s not all! Capping it all off is a dangerous forbidden romance. <br /><br />I’m sold! I need to start another series like I need a hole in head, and I loathe the idea of binge reading, but I’m signing on for this one all the way. <br /><br />Can’t wait to read the next book!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12602693437937119237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1439577247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1439577247" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1439577247?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1439577247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11842022818403502358"><b>3.5 (ish) stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Don't fear the reaper. Just be very, very aware of her.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Well, personally, I have <b>mixed feelings</b> towards the reaper.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381583386ra/5066701.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Confused. Befuddled. Puzzled. Disconcerted. Call it what you like, it's still the same. While <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson___1_' title='First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson, #1) by Darynda Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>First Grave on the Right</a> was <b>a gripping and funny story</b>, I had some issues with it, especially with Charley.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460810790ra/18791459.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let's take it from the start.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just a girl, a few ghosts, and the entire human race. What could be easier?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>The creepy guy we call the reaper is</span>
  <span id="freeText11842022818403502358" style="display:none"><b>3.5 (ish) stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Don't fear the reaper. Just be very, very aware of her.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Well, personally, I have <b>mixed feelings</b> towards the reaper.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381583386ra/5066701.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Confused. Befuddled. Puzzled. Disconcerted. Call it what you like, it's still the same. While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson___1_" title="First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson, #1) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">First Grave on the Right</a> was <b>a gripping and funny story</b>, I had some issues with it, especially with Charley.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460810790ra/18791459.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's take it from the start.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Just a girl, a few ghosts, and the entire human race. What could be easier?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The creepy guy we call the reaper is not that creepy after all. Nor a guy. Charley Davidson, a Private Investigator that always, <i>always</i> gets into trouble, has a second, more important job: she ferries souls to the other side, and sometimes helps them deal with their unfinished business, meaning she investigates their murders. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8788554.First_Grave_on_the_Right__Charley_Davidson___1_" title="First Grave on the Right (Charley Davidson, #1) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">First Grave on the Right</a>, three lawyers were killed because of a case and Charley, her Uncle Bob and the rest of the APD search for the men responsible. For Charley, it means getting beaten up, falling from warehouses, almost getting killed etc etc while she tries to solve the mystery that cloaks the sexy man that visits her dreams and now becomes a part of her reality. And when I say sexy, I mean <i>really</i> sexy.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Reyes Farrow.<br>Because perfection is a dirty job, but someone has to do it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349102ra/703202.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But we'll talk about this sexy devil later.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Better to see dead than be dead.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4175419.Darynda_Jones" title="Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Darynda Jones</a> certainly knows how to write a helluva entertaining book!</b> There were so many times my shoulders shook from <b>laughter</b>, I loved the <b>sass</b> and the <b>banters</b> and the way Charley handled the dead people! Hell, I loved all the dead people, from Angel to Demon Child! <b>But</b>, there are some buts. At some points my head hurt from the struggle to understand what the hell was going on, and later there was such an info-dump that my head also hurt from the struggle to process the information! I liked the <b>crime aspect</b>, it kept me on edge and was never boring, but the conclusion of this case felt a little <b>underwhelming</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471855789ra/20114391.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then there is Charley. <b>I couldn't help but compare her to Kate Daniels, and found her lacking</b>. Kate Daniels? She's insubordinate, and smart and kicks some ass, in an I-wanna-be-you way. Charley Davidson? She's <b>borderline ridiculous</b>, <b>slightly annoying</b> and <b>unrealistic</b>, a cheap imitation. Her bravado and cockiness almost drove me nuts, she tried hard to convince everyone that she's a badass, while <b>
  <i>Kate is genuinely a badass</i>
</b>. I'm sorry Charley, but you acted like a child trying to impress the adults. And I was not impressed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462572690ra/19016162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Except Garrett, who was a total douchebag, I liked the secondary characters! They had attitude, they were witty and a great addition to the story! And then comes Reyes. <b>Hot damn!</b> The parts I enjoyed the most were the ones where Charley tried to discover the secrets about his past. While his true identity took me by surprise and there are yet many things to learn about him, his presence affected me the way it affected Charley! <b>Hot damn!</b> Well, to be honest, Charley was constantly horny, but her chemistry with Reyes was off the charts, and I may have drooled a little. Just a little.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444158161ra/16460595.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As you can tell, there were many pros and cons. I will continue with Charley Davidson's adventures in the future, but that's not a priority for the time being. <b>I do recommend this series if you're in for a fun, sexy paranormal story full of action and laughter!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11842022818403502358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_186363572" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186363572" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186363572?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who are looking for a hot and hilarious summer read</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lora by: </span>
      Dawn, Maja, J.R. Ward, my library's shelving system
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186363572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13432354816140673708">. . . So. I was browsing in the New Fiction shelves at my library the other day — you know, just like every bookaholic does — and I came across debut author Darynda Jones' <i>First Grave on the Right</i>. I flipped through it, thought it sounded interesting but decided to put it back for the moment, since my bag was already giving me a shoulder cramp. Just as I was putting it back on the shelf, I noticed the blurb on the cover: <i>"The best debut novel I've read in years! Hilarious and heartfelt, sexy and</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13432354816140673708" style="display:none">. . . So. I was browsing in the New Fiction shelves at my library the other day — you know, just like every bookaholic does — and I came across debut author Darynda Jones' <i>First Grave on the Right</i>. I flipped through it, thought it sounded interesting but decided to put it back for the moment, since my bag was already giving me a shoulder cramp. Just as I was putting it back on the shelf, I noticed the blurb on the cover: <i>"The best debut novel I've read in years! Hilarious and heartfelt, sexy and surprising. An absolute must-read!"</i> — <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/20248.J_R__Ward" title="J.R. Ward" rel="nofollow noopener">J.R. Ward</a><br />And my first thought was, <i>J.R. Ward? Sold!</i> So, twenty-pound, shoulder-cramping book bag in hand, I headed to the library's check out — and what a great decision that turned out to be.<br /><br />Our main character, Charley, has been gifted (or cursed, depending on how the onlooker chooses to see it) with the ability to see the dead since birth. But that isn't all she does: Charley is the grim reaper. She helps the dead pass on to the other side. <br />At a very young age Charley began helping her father, a currently retired police detective, solve murder cases. Today, she continues this line of work as a private investigator, working with Uncle Bob. It's a lot easier to solve a crime when you know who the murderer is or where the body is stashed.<br />To top this off, Charley's had to deal with an evil stepmother because her biological mother died giving birth to her. As you can image, Charley's life hasn't been an easy one. But she seems to take it all in stride.<br /><br />Charley is quite the character. She's very sassy and snarky, but underneath that she has a lot of heart. You can't help but like her and wish you had friend with her spirit and attitude.<br />And what to say about the mysterious and alluring Reyes? I won't spoil the nature of what Reyes truly is, but it is a little bit of a shocker. The book's synopsis kind of makes it sound like Reyes is an incubus . . . but I won't say what he is. Just know that it is fairly original when compared to all of the vampires and werewolves, and that this reader looks forward to delving into his character more in the sequel.<br /><br />One of the best things about this book is that there is a nice helping of <b>HUMOR</b>. There hasn't been nearly enough humor in my reading regimen lately, but <i>First Grave on the Right</i> has brought back the humor for me and I'm enjoying the stomach pain.<br /><br />Just check out some of these quotes:<br /><br /><i>"I awoke at the butt crack of dawn with the call of nature urging me out of bed."<br /><br />"I went down like a drunken cowgirl trying to line dance to Metallica."<br /><br />"I once signed up for an anger management class, but the instructor pissed me off."</i><br /><br />And there's plenty more where those came from.<br /><br />This book was just fabulous. And you know what is even <i>more</i> fabulous? The fact that I only have to wait until August 16th to read its sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9565045.Second_Grave_on_the_Left__Charley_Davidson___2_" title="Second Grave on the Left (Charley Davidson, #2) by Darynda Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Second Grave on the Left</a>.<br /><br />People looking for a feel-good, funny, sexy summer read should really enjoy <i>First Grave on the Right</i>.<br /><br />P.S. I am envious of the cover model's feet. Or foot, as the case may be.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13432354816140673708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144164033" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144164033" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144164033?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780749956042" href="/book/show/11357769-first-grave-on-the-right">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=books-for-rainy-days">books-for-rainy-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144164033" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12991282796874436444"><i>Garrett chose that moment to join the conversation. “I appreciate your forethought,” he said, his tone distant, as if his mind were elsewhere. “Not as much as your fore-<b>parts</b>, but still…”<br/>I twisted around in my seat to face him. “My fore-parts, as you so ineloquently put it, have names.” I pointed to my right breast. “This is Danger.” Then my left. “And this is Will Robinson. I would appreciate it if you addressed them accordingly.”<br/>After a long pause in which he took the time to blink several tim</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12991282796874436444" style="display:none"><i>Garrett chose that moment to join the conversation. “I appreciate your forethought,” he said, his tone distant, as if his mind were elsewhere. “Not as much as your fore-<b>parts</b>, but still…”<br />I twisted around in my seat to face him. “My fore-parts, as you so ineloquently put it, have names.” I pointed to my right breast. “This is Danger.” Then my left. “And this is Will Robinson. I would appreciate it if you addressed them accordingly.”<br />After a long pause in which he took the time to blink several times, he asked, “You named your breasts?”<br />I turned my back to him with a shrug. “I named my ovaries, too, but they don’t get out as much.”</i><br /><br />Now, if that little quote didn’t convince you to read First Grave on the Right, nothing I write will, either. <br /><br />There's a new generation of UF authors who are slowly but surely rising to the throne. The names that instantly come to mind are Nicole Peeler, Jaye Wells and now Darynda Jones. I think it’s a lot harder to succeed these days than it was for Charlaine Harris, Patricia Briggs or Ilona Andrews, for example. It has become very difficult to find something new and exciting to read in the ocean of new UF novels. Yes, ladies and gentlemen, we’ve seen it all and a completely original story is now a distant dream. I guess there are two ways around that obstacle. The first is finding something never before used, which is (as I’ve already said) almost impossible. Nicole Peeler did it, sure, but she IS a college professor, and all professors are generally awesome.<br /> The second would be developing a great sense of humor (if you don’t already have one) and using it to distinguish yourself. That’s the path Darynda Jones chose, and she was extremely successful. The best way to start a book is with a laugh. Jones obviously knows this. By making the reader laugh on the very first page, the author achieves two important goals: he/she makes the MC instantly likeable and because of that, the reader keeps turning those pages.<br /><br />I’ve read a couple of reviews comparing Jones to Janet Evanovich. Having just recently finished Wicked Appetite, I think that the only thing they have in common is that they are both hilarious. Although First Grave on the Right certainly is a fun read and Jones undoubtedly has a fantastic sense of humor, she does not have Evanovich’s courage to just let go: abandon all rules and reason along the way. But unlike Wicked Appetite, First Grave on the Right has a solid story that holds all the humor together. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12991282796874436444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_137796303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137796303" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137796303?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781429993265" href="/book/show/10333518-first-grave-on-the-right">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137796303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7073184307717485794">Don't you just love it when the majority of your friends love a book and keep telling you to read it but for some reason you don't get around to it. Then when you finally do...the only question that begs asking is why didn't I read this sooner?? That's this book exactly! <br/><br/>But <i>beware</i>...if you do not like snark, do not read this book. It is loaded with snark with more snark on top and even some snark sprinkles but any girl that names her boobs "Danger" and "Will Robinson" and her ovaries, "Beam me </span>
  <span id="freeText7073184307717485794" style="display:none">Don't you just love it when the majority of your friends love a book and keep telling you to read it but for some reason you don't get around to it. Then when you finally do...the only question that begs asking is why didn't I read this sooner?? That's this book exactly! <br><br>But <i>beware</i>...if you do not like snark, do not read this book. It is loaded with snark with more snark on top and even some snark sprinkles but any girl that names her boobs "Danger" and "Will Robinson" and her ovaries, "Beam me up" and "Scotty" is A-OK in my book. <br><br>Charley is a private investigator and works closely with the Albuquerque police department (namely her Uncle Bob who is a Detective) but she is also The Grim Reaper and her main job is to help dead people pass to the other side. This is a bonus for Charley in that she can often talk to victims and help solve their crimes. <br><br>I really enjoyed Charley and thought she was hilarious. It was great that there were things she didn't know or understand and that she was doing a lot of things on the fly. The one thing that was a bit strange was that she is described as being 'sparkly' as in the light she gives off being the Grim Reaper aka portal. It just gave me a weird <i>Twilight</i> vibe. <br><br>Charley has an assistant who is her best friend and who also lives right across the hall from her named Cookie. Cookie is the best friend <i>ever</i>. She is always there for Charley and accepts her as she is. I really enjoyed her but would have liked to get more 'about' her. <br><br>Of course, there are a couple of men. Garrett Swopes is a skiptracer (think bounty hunter) and while taken back about Charley in the beginning, it does seem that he is coming around. And then there is Reyes...hot, hot, hot Reyes. and did I mention intense? hot and intense and <i>naughty</i>!! That's right...naughty. And right from the start we find out that nightly he is trying to get into Charley's pants and doing a darn fine job! The problem is he's only doing that in her dreams. <br><br>Here's a little visual....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1299200899p8/227273.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Yep...Reyes is no Gandy Candy...he's hot and earthy and <u>growly</u>. He's a big part of the story and we find out lots of interesting things about him as does Charley. I have a <i>mighty need</i> to know why he calls her 'Dutch'. <br><br>Of course, there is a police case going on and things do get a bit muddled. It's just that's there so much going on and so many characters but the good part is that towards the end, you should have a good grip on things. I'm sure this will make the next books much easier. <br><br>The other part that needs mentioning is the chapter titles with the tshirt and bumper sticker sayings. A couple of my favorites are:<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Never knock on death’s door. Ring the doorbell then run. He totally hates that. —T-SHIRT<br><br>I may not look like much, but I’m an expert at pretending to be a ninja. —BUMPER STICKER<br><br></b>
</blockquote><br><br>LOVED the ending and definitely a fine start to what seems to be a great series. <i>Twenty lashes with a wet noodle accepted.</i><br><br><br>Favorite quotes: <br><br>♦ “Were you just possessed?” Cookie asked after a long moment, awe softening her voice. “ ’Cause let me tell you, sweetheart, if that was possession, I’m selling my soul.”<br><br>♥ "Why does the Earth seek the warmth of the sun?” My brows slid together, trying to understand. “Or the forest seek the embrace of the rain?”</span>
  <a data-text-id="7073184307717485794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer18192219163649684639"><b>HA! What a crazy-fun read!</b> Definitely <b>not</b> my usual fare, and honestly, I almost threw in the towel...more than once...prior to the half-way point, but then Reyes, his difficult family life and the <b>BIG BAD</b> caught my attention.<p>PI Charlotte "Charley" Davidson is a 27 year old beauty. She drives a jeep named Misery..."in honor of the master of horror"...has a cop for an uncle...an ex-cop for a dad, and an evil step-mother. Most importantly, though, she has very special abilities...abilities not ever</p></span>
  <span id="freeText18192219163649684639" style="display:none"><b>HA! What a crazy-fun read!</b> Definitely <b>not</b> my usual fare, and honestly, I almost threw in the towel...more than once...prior to the half-way point, but then Reyes, his difficult family life and the <b>BIG BAD</b> caught my attention.<p>PI Charlotte "Charley" Davidson is a 27 year old beauty. She drives a jeep named Misery..."in honor of the master of horror"...has a cop for an uncle...an ex-cop for a dad, and an evil step-mother. Most importantly, though, she has very special abilities...abilities not everyone believes. <b>SHE SEES GHOSTS</b>....talks to ghosts...and even acts as a portal to the other side.</p><p>Most of Charley's other-worldly friends are pleasant and just want help...answers...or to deliver messages to those left behind, but one presence in her life is dark, creepy....a huge cloaked figure who sweeps in and around her....and another who enters her dreams....is dangerously mysterious....irresistibly sensual....and ultimately her protector.</p><p>Charley Davidson in many ways reminds me of Janet Evanovich's Stephanie Plum. Working cases in conjunction with the police....great sidekicks <i>(love Cookie &amp; Angel)</i>....cracking wise....ALWAYS getting into trouble....AND having lots of hot sex!</p><p><b>FIRST GRAVE ON THE RIGHT</b> is an entertaining read albeit, overall, a bit too light for me. I truly like my ghosts super creepy-scary - - - LIKE THE SECRET WE DISCOVER IN THE END, hehehe.</p><p>3.5 Stars with a roundup to 4.0. Just might have to read one more!</p><p>Many thanks to St. Martin's Press and NetGalley for the complimentary reading opportunity.</p></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8307376435493359855">Snark, snark, grim reaper, snark, light mystery, hot supernatural sex, snark.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557929639ra/27513058.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I alternated between listening to this one via Libby and reading a digital review copy. Narrator Lorelei King does a phenomenal job with the voices in this, and she nails the snark levels. A new fave narrator to add to my list :)<br/><br/>I raced through this book and barely caught my breath before jumping into the second book in the series! Charley is a very fun character and I cannot wait to spend more time with her. <br/><br/>There were</span>
  <span id="freeText8307376435493359855" style="display:none">Snark, snark, grim reaper, snark, light mystery, hot supernatural sex, snark.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1557929639ra/27513058.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I alternated between listening to this one via Libby and reading a digital review copy. Narrator Lorelei King does a phenomenal job with the voices in this, and she nails the snark levels. A new fave narrator to add to my list :)<br><br>I raced through this book and barely caught my breath before jumping into the second book in the series! Charley is a very fun character and I cannot wait to spend more time with her. <br><br>There were a few brief moments in this book when the snark was almost trying too hard, but it certainly wasn't enough to put me off. The sex is pretty steamy, but didn't quite get to the point of potentially uncomfortable smuttiness. The amusing moments far outweighed the awkward.<br><br>4.5 snarky stars rounded up for this one!<br><br><i>Thanks to NetGalley and St. Martin's Press for providing me with a DRC of this book.</i></span>

<div id="review_1269591910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1269591910" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1269591910?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with">girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1269591910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4934723698147598626">2016 is the year of 5-stars for me. I used to be so picky about handing out the 5-star rating, but then I realized that life is too short to be stingy with the stars. If I like it a lot, then all the stars for you! YOLO! (sorry for saying YOLO, but YOLO)<br/><br/>So, this book is like a rom-com that is more com, with the MC being the Grim Reaper. A sarcastic, funny, slightly crazy Grim Reaper. Who is a private investigator, because why not? She sees dead people and that is very helpful in murder investiga</span>
  <span id="freeText4934723698147598626" style="display:none">2016 is the year of 5-stars for me. I used to be so picky about handing out the 5-star rating, but then I realized that life is too short to be stingy with the stars. If I like it a lot, then all the stars for you! YOLO! (sorry for saying YOLO, but YOLO)<br><br>So, this book is like a rom-com that is more com, with the MC being the Grim Reaper. A sarcastic, funny, slightly crazy Grim Reaper. Who is a private investigator, because why not? She sees dead people and that is very helpful in murder investigations. They can just tell her who murdered them. Convenient, right? Putting away bad guys is totally worth having dead people constantly talking to her and making her look crazier. And, the requests they have for her...<br><br><b>
  <i>He asked, "In the meantime, can I jump in your body and make out with my wife through you?"<br><br>I fought a grin. "It doesn't really work that way."<br><br>"Then can you just make out with my wife and pretend I'm in your body?"<br><br>"No."<br><br>"I can pay. I have money."<br><br>"How much we talking?"</i>
</b><br><br>Can't help loving a girl who is willing to be bribed! For the right price, I'll make out with the dead guy's wife.<br><br>So, Charley is trying to help three dead lawyers find their murderer while also trying to get their former client free from a false murder charge. I know, I know, three dead lawyers and no lawyer joke? Come on now. What would we do without lawyers?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454666552i/17996232.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>well, there's that...</i><br><br>At the same time, Charley is trying to help her comatose dream-lover, who happens to be in prison, stay alive because the state is planning on pulling his plug - you know, being brain-dead and all. But, for a brain-dead guy, he is still managing to have sex with Charley in some weird, out-of-body dream experience. I know, I know, a brain-dead guy having sex and no joke? Come on now. Where would we be without brain-dead fuckboys?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454666552i/17996233.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>okay, that would be nice...</i><br><br>And, while working these cases, Charley is constantly getting beat-up, and multiple attempts are made on her life. But, Charley has the best attitude throughout. She is half-dead, but still making jokes and crawling in to work. I love that she's NOT a badass. She constantly gets her ass kicked. But, that she keeps this positive attitude and her fun spirit in spite of it all.<br><br><b>
  <i>I doubted anyone was in the mood to laugh. Besides me. Laughing was like Jell-O. There was always room for Jell-O.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454666552i/17996234.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>well, I certainly couldn't resist this one, could I?</i><br><br>I had so much fun reading this book that Charley is going on my Book BFF list. I want to hang out with her and Cookie. We can do Jell-O shots and play tricks on dead people. That would be fun!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4934723698147598626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer673256431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1174114744882727671"><b>Sale Alert January Book Deal for $2.99 on <a href='https://www.amazon.com/First-Grave-Right-Charley-Davidson-ebook/dp/B0044781TW/ref=sr_1_5?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1514831674&sr=1-5' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a></b><br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“If I couldn't be a good example, I'd just have to be a horrible warning.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I want to be Charley Davidson….I can’t say that I have ever read a book and was like omg I want to be that girl. I mean I love characters in other books don’t get me wrong but who really wants to <i>be</i> Katness, or Georgina Kincaid, okay okay I maybe want to be MacKayla Lane (cuz seriously Barons would be worth it) but I totally wanted to be Charley. If it wasn’t for</span>
  <span id="freeText1174114744882727671" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert January Book Deal for $2.99 on <a href="https://www.amazon.com/First-Grave-Right-Charley-Davidson-ebook/dp/B0044781TW/ref=sr_1_5?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1514831674&amp;sr=1-5" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a></b><br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“If I couldn't be a good example, I'd just have to be a horrible warning.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I want to be Charley Davidson….I can’t say that I have ever read a book and was like omg I want to be that girl. I mean I love characters in other books don’t get me wrong but who really wants to <i>be</i> Katness, or Georgina Kincaid, okay okay I maybe want to be MacKayla Lane (cuz seriously Barons would be worth it) but I totally wanted to be Charley. If it wasn’t for the fact that it appears to be Kill Charley Davidson week I think I’d consider it seriously. We are already both addicted to coffee and not morning people so I’m like 8% on my way already. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You called me at four thirty-four....I hate four thirty-four. I think four thirty-four should be banned and replaced with something more reasonable, like, say, nine twelve.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Not only is she the most quick witted, snarky, smart and absolutely funny character I read, I mean she named her breasts Danger and Will Robinson, she is also having hot, the heavens open up and choirs sing halleluiah, sex every night in her dreams with talk dark and masculine. Not to mention the fact that she is a Private Investigator that helps solve crimes, see ghosts because she is also a Grim Reaper and she has death incarnate as a protector. Like I said bad ass<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“My calculations - allowing for a 12 percent margin of error, based on the radius of the corresponding confidence interval and the surgeon general's warning - concluded that they (ghosts) probably didn't stay behind for the tacos.”</i>
</b> <br /><br />The story was totally different than anything I thought it would be. I mean sure she helps people that have been murdered or have lingering business on this side find closure so they can cross over to the other side, nothing really unusual there. But, the intertwined story of finding the man from her dreams….well let me just say that I didn’t see that one coming at all. The story behind Reyes, the man in her bed did not go even close to the direction I thought it would and I was floored by the big reveal of who and what he was. That doesn’t happen to me very often, I usually clue in ahead of time.<br /><br />All the side characters were entertaining and the banter absolutely the funniest dialog I’ve read between characters. Her sex obsessed secretary and neighbor Cookie, Swopes fellow PI who is having a hard time believing in her gift, her Uncle on the police force she helps solve crimes all were great sounding boards for Charley and her unique dialog. She had so many great one liners that it was absolutely charmingly hilarious. I wish I could get away with saying half the stuff she did.<br /><br />If you are looking for a strong heroine who is smart, funny, charming and doesn’t take crap from anyone this is right up your ally. This is one of the strongest ratings I’ve given to a book at the beginning of a series. I can’t wait to see what else is in store for Charley.</span>
